فأما الملتقط فلم أر من بين شرائطه ولا يشترط بلوغه بدليل ما في المجتبى التعريف إلى ولي الصبي والوارث اهـ. فدل على صحة التقاطه. وأما حرية الملتقط فليست بشرط لأن للعبد يداً صحيحة بدليل قولهم كما في البزازية من الوديعة ليس للمالك أن يأخذ وديعة عبده مأذوناً أم لا ما لم يحضر ويظهر أنه من كسبه لاحتمال أن تكون وديعة الغير في يد العبد، فإن للعبد تدفع إليه اهـ . لكن قدمنا أنه لو التقط لقيطاً فقال المولى هو عبدي وقال العبد التقطته فإن محجوراً فالقول للمولى و إن مأذوناً فللعبد ولم أر حكم اللقطة إذا تنازعا فيها وينبغي أن يكون كذلك، ولم أر حكم تعريف لقطته هل إليه أو إلى مولاه، وإذا عرفت فهل يتملكها المولى إن كان فقيراً؟ وهل يتوقف الالتقاط على إذن المولى؟ وهل الإذن في التجارة إذن في الالتقاط؟ وهل المكاتب كالحر أو العبد فيه؟ ثم رأيت في الكافي للحاكم عن أبي سعيد مولى أبي رشيد قال : وجدت خمسمائة درهم بالحيرة وأنا مكاتب قال فذكرت ذلك لعمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه فقال اعمل بها وعرفها قال : فعملت بها حتى أديت مكاتبتي ثم أتيته فأخبرته فقال : ادفعها إلى خزائن بيت المال اهـ . وسيأتي أن العبد لورد الآبق فالجعل لمولاه فينبغي أن يكون أهلاً للالتقاط، وأن المولى يعرفها ثم يتملكها إن كان فقيراً. وأما إسلام الملتقط فليس بشرط بدليل ما في الكافي للحاكم : لو أقام مدعيها شهوداً كفاراً على ملتقط کافر قبلت اهـ. فدل على صحة التقاط الكافر وعلى هذا تثبت الأحكام من التعريف والتصدق بعده أو الانتفاع ولم أره صريحاً، ولم أر حكم التقاط المرتد لقيطاً أو لقطة والظاهر أن مشايخنا إنما لم يقيدوا الملتقط بشيء لإطلاقه عندنا
As for the finder, I have not specified his conditions; adulthood is not required according to what is in al-Mujtaba: the announcement is made to the guardian of the child and heir. So it indicates the validity of his picking up. As for the freedom of the finder, it is not a condition because the slave has a valid hand as evidence of their statement in al-Bazzaziyyah: the trust (وديعة) – the owner cannot take the trust of his slave, whether permitted or not, unless he is present and it is apparent it is from his earnings, because it may be a trust of another in the slave's hand; for the slave, it is given to him. But we have previously stated that if he picks up a foundling and the master says 'It is my slave' and the slave says 'I picked it up', then if the slave is restricted (محجور), the master's word is taken; if permitted, the slave's word. I have not seen the ruling of the latta when they dispute over it; it should be similar. I have not seen the ruling of the announcement of his found property: is it to him or to his master? And if it is announced, does the master own it if he is poor? Does the picking up depend on the master's permission? Is permission for trade permission for picking up? Is the mukatib like a free person or a slave in this? Then I saw in al-Kafi al-Hakim from Abu Sa'id Mawla Abi Rashid who said: I found five hundred dirhams in al-Hira while I was a mukatib. I mentioned that to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA), and he said: Use it and announce it. So I used it until I paid off my kitabah, then I came to him and informed him. He said: Pay it to the treasury of the Muslims. It will come that the slave who finds a runaway slave – the fee belongs to his master, so it should be that the master is eligible for picking up, that the master announces it then owns it if he is poor. As for the Islam of the finder, it is not a condition based on the evidence in al-Kafi al-Hakim: if the claimant brings disbelieving witnesses against a disbelieving finder, it is accepted. So it indicates the validity of a disbeliever's picking up, and upon this, the rulings of announcement, giving charity thereafter, or benefiting are established. I have not seen it explicitly, and I have not seen the ruling of an apostate's picking up of a foundling or lost property, and the apparent view is that our scholars did not restrict the finder to anything due to its generality with us.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions (شرائط) required for a person to be considered a valid finder (ملتقط) of lost property. The author begins by stating that he has not specified conditions for the finder, indicating that the Hanafi school is lenient. He then addresses three specific potential conditions: adulthood (بلوغ), freedom (حرية), and Islam (إسلام). 

1. **Adulthood**: The author cites al-Mujtaba that the announcement (تعريف) is made to the guardian of a child and the heir, implying that a minor can validly pick up lost property. Thus, puberty is not required.
2. **Freedom**: The author argues that a slave has a valid legal hand (يد صحيحة) based on a ruling from al-Bazzaziyyah: the owner cannot take a trust deposited with his slave because the slave's hand is considered valid. Therefore, a slave can pick up lost property. However, disputes between master and slave regarding foundlings are handled differently: if the slave is restricted (محجور), the master's claim prevails; if permitted (مأذون), the slave's claim prevails. The author leaves open questions about announcements and ownership for the poor master.
3. **Islam**: The author cites al-Kafi al-Hakim that witnesses from disbelievers are accepted against a disbelieving finder, proving that a non-Muslim can validly pick up lost property. However, he questions the ruling for an apostate (مرتد).

The passage also discusses mukatib (a slave who has contracted to buy his freedom), referencing the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab with a mukatib finder. The mukatib is treated like a free person in this context? Actually the narration supports the mukatib's ability to manage the found item, but eventually it goes to the treasury. The overall conclusion is that the Hanafi madhhab does not restrict the finder; anyone with a valid hand can pick up lost property.

Key Terms
الملتقط (al-multaqit): The person who picks up lost property.
التعريف (al-ta'rif): The announcement or public declaration of finding lost property, required to be made.
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract to gain freedom by paying installments.
المحجور (al-mahjur): A person under legal interdiction, here a restricted slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab
D) Consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi madhhab, the finder of lost property does not need to be an adult, free, or Muslim; any person with a valid legal hand may validly pick up and is obligated to announce.

Luqatah — Found Property

Finder's Right: No Priority Over Another Finder
Compares first finder's right with second finder for lost property vs foundling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not grant the first finder of lost property priority over a second finder, and distinguish this from the case of a foundling.

Core Idea
First finder of lost property has no priority over a later finder — unlike a foundling.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key principle in the law of lost property (luqatah). If you find a lost item and later see it in someone else’s hands, you cannot simply reclaim it by virtue of having been the first finder. The Hanafi school considers all finders equal in terms of custody, because the true owner is unknown. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and contrasts it with the finder of a foundling, who does gain a superior right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule from al-Walwaljiyyah
State the core ruling: if a lost item is taken by one person, lost, and then found in another’s possession, there is no lawsuit between them.
The text explicitly says: 'فلا خصومة بينه وبين ذلك الرجل'.
2
Understand the Reasoning
The second finder is like the first in taking the lost property, because both have a ‘hand’ (yad) over it. There is no priority.
The key phrase: 'الثاني في أخذ اللقطة كالأول'.
3
Compare with Trust (Wadi‘a) and Foundling (Laqit)
In a trust (amana), the original trustee has a superior right; in foundling, the first finder gains a right of custody. Lost property differs because it has an apparent owner (the unknown owner).
The difference hinges on whether there is another apparent claimant.
4
Examine the Problematic Scenario
Consider if the first finder had the item forcibly taken. The first finder still has the right to own it after announcement if poor – but that right is against the original owner, not against a subsequent finder.
The author raises this to show that the first finder's right is not absolute.
5
Conclude the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position: the first finder cannot sue the second because their possession is equal; the second’s taking is a fresh custody.
This ruling applies when the item was lost from the first and then found by the second.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الولوالجية : رجل التقط لقطة فضاعت منه ثم وجدها في يد رجل فلا خصومة بينه وبين ذلك الرجل فرق بينه وبين الوديعة، والفرق أن الثاني في أخذ اللقطة كالأول وليس الثاني في أخذ الوديعة كالأول. ولو التقط الرجل لقيطاً فأخذه منه رجل ثم اختصما فيه فالأول أحق به لأن الأول صار أحق بإمساكه بحكم اليد لأنه ليس له مستحق آخر بحسب الظاهر لأنه لو كان له مستحق وجد مطروحاً من حيث الظاهر ولا كذلك اللقطة لأن لها مستحقاً آخر من حيث الظاهر فلا يثبت الاستحقاق لصاحب اليد الأول فكان الثاني في إثبات اليد كالأول .اهـ. فقد علمت أن الملتقط ليس أحق بها وهو مشكل لو انتزعها إنسان منه غصباً فإنه يثبت للأول حق أن يتملكها بعد التعريف لو كان فقيراً فكيف يبطله الثاني؟ نعم لو ضاعت من الأول والتقطها آخر فإن الأول لا يخاصمه لأنها لقطة للثاني والأول لا يملك الخصومة، ولا يقال إن كلامهم فيما إذا ضاعت
In al-Walwaljiyyah: A man picked up a lost item, it was lost from him, then he found it in the hand of another man – there is no litigation between him and that other man. There is a difference between this and the trust (وديعة). The difference is that the second in taking the lost item is like the first, but the second in taking the trust is not like the first. If a man picks up a foundling and another man takes it from him, then they dispute over it, the first is more entitled because the first has become more entitled to its custody by virtue of possession (يد), as there is no other apparent entitled person. But this is not so for the lost item because the lost item has another entitled person apparent. Thus, the first finder is not established entitled, so the second is like the first in establishing possession. Therefore, you have learned that the finder of lost property is not more entitled to it. This is problematic: if someone takes it from him by force, the first still has the right to own it after announcement if he is poor; how can the second invalidate it? Yes, if it is lost from the first and another picks it up, the first does not litigate because it is a lost item for the second, and the first does not have standing to litigate. It is not said that their statement applies to when it was lost.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage compares the finder's right to a lost object (لقطة) versus a foundling (لقيط). The author cites al-Walwaljiyyah: if a person picks up a lost item, then loses it, and later finds it in someone else's hands, there is no lawsuit between them because the second finder has as much right as the first. However, in the case of a trust (وديعة), the original trustee has a superior right. For a foundling, the first finder is more entitled to custody because the foundling has no apparent other claimant; the first finder's possession establishes a right. In contrast, lost property has an apparent owner (the unknown owner), so the first finder does not gain a superior right; the second finder is equal. The author then raises a problem: if someone forcibly takes the lost item from the first finder, the first still has the right to own it after announcement if poor. How can the second's taking invalidate the first? He answers that if it is lost from the first and then found by another, the first has no lawsuit because the property is now in the second's hands, and the first is not a claimant. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main point is clear: the finder of lost property is not uniquely entitled, unlike the finder of a foundling.

Key Terms
الخصومة (al-khusumah): Litigation or legal claim arising from possession of lost property.
اللقيط (al-laqit): Foundling (abandoned child). In this context, compared to lost property, the first finder has superior right.
اليد (al-yad): Possession or control; in fiqh, possession creates certain rights. However, for lost property, mere possession does not give priority over another possessor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Walwaljiyyah, if a person picks up a lost item, loses it, and then finds it in the hands of another person, what is the ruling?
A) The first person can sue to get it back
B) There is no litigation because the second taker is like the first
C) The first person is entitled to it because of prior possession
D) The item should be given to the first person if he is poor

Key Takeaway
The first finder of lost property has no legal priority over a second finder; both are equal custodians for the unknown owner.

Luqatah — Found Property

The Finder's Right to the Luqta vs. Another Person
Explains the ruling when a luqta is lost and found by another, and the difference with a foundling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a luqta is lost and found by another, and distinguish it from the rulings on a foundling (laqit) and a deposit (wadi'a).

Core Idea
If a found luqta is lost and found by another, the first finder loses all rights – the second finder steps into his shoes exactly.

This passage from al-Walwaljiyya addresses a critical scenario: what happens when a finder loses a luqta and it is picked up by someone else? The author explains that the first finder cannot claim it from the second, because in the eyes of the law, the second is like the first. He contrasts this with a deposit (wadi'a) and a foundling (laqit) to clarify the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A man finds a luqta, then loses it, and another man finds it. The first finder sees it in the second's possession and claims it.
2
State the ruling
There is no litigation between them (la khusumata). The first finder cannot sue the second for return.
The text says: 'فلا خصومة بينه وبين ذلك الرجل'
3
Compare with wadi'a (deposit)
If the item were a deposit, the first holder (trustee) would have the right to reclaim it from a second finder, because the deposit is still owed to the owner. For luqta, the second finder is not liable to the first.
The difference is that the second in taking a deposit is not like the first.
4
Compare with laqit (foundling)
If a foundling is taken by a second person, the first finder remains the rightful custodian. The first becomes entitled by virtue of first possession, as there is no other apparent guardian.
For luqta, there is an apparent owner (the original loser), so the first finder does not get exclusive right.
5
Understand the rationale
Luqta has a known or potential owner (its original owner) in appearance, so the first finder does not acquire a permanent right. Laqit has no visible owner, so the first finder's custody is protected.
The text: 'لأن اللقطة لها مستحق آخر من حيث الظاهر'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الولوالجية : رجل التقط لقطة فضاعت منه ثم وجدها في يد رجل فلا خصومة بينه وبين ذلك الرجل فرق بينه وبين الوديعة، والفرق أن الثاني في أخذ اللقطة كالأول وليس الثاني في أخذ الوديعة كالأول. ولو التقط الرجل لقيطاً فأخذه منه رجل ثم اختصما فيه فالأول أحق به لأن الأول صار أحق بإمساكه بحكم اليد لأنه ليس له مستحق آخر بحسب الظاهر لأنه لو كان له مستحق وجد مطروحاً من حيث الظاهر ولا كذلك اللقطة لأن لها مستحقاً آخر من حيث الظاهر فلا يثبت الاستحقاق لصاحب اليد الأول فكان الثاني في إثبات اليد كالأول .اهـ. فقد علمت أن الملتقط ليس أحق بها وهو مشكل لو انتزعها إنسان منه غصباً فإنه يثبت للأول حق أن يتملكها بعد التعريف لو كان فقيراً فكيف يبطله الثاني؟ نعم لو ضاعت من الأول والتقطها آخر فإن الأول لا يخاصمه لأنها لقطة للثاني والأول لا يملك الخصومة، ولا يقال إن كلامهم فيما إذا ضاعت لأنا نقول : قد بينا أنهما مسألتان : الأولى فيما إذا ضاعت وفرقوا بينها وبين الوديعة الثانية فيما إذا أخذها رجل منه وفرقوا بينها وبين اللقيط وأما اللقطة فلا فرق عندنا ولقطة كما أفاده بقوله وصح التقاطه البهيمة ولا فرق بين مكان ومكان كما أفاده بقوله
And in al-Walwaljiyya: A man found a luqta and it was lost from him, then he found it in the hand of another man, so there is no litigation between him and that man. They made a difference between it and a deposit. The difference is that the second in taking the luqta is like the first, but the second in taking a deposit is not like the first. And if a man found a foundling (laqit) and another man took it from him, then they dispute over it, the first is more entitled to it because the first became more entitled to keep it by virtue of possession, since there is no other rightful claimant in appearance. Because if there were a rightful claimant, it would be found abandoned in appearance. Not so for the luqta, because it has another rightful claimant in appearance, so entitlement is not established for the first possessor. Thus the second in establishing possession is like the first. So you know that the finder is not more entitled to it. This is problematic if someone takes it from him forcibly, for the first has the right to own it after announcing if he is poor, so how can the second invalidate that? Yes, if it is lost from the first and another finds it, the first does not litigate him because it is a luqta for the second and the first does not have standing to litigate. And it is not said that their statement concerns when it is lost, for we say: We have explained that they are two issues: first, when it is lost, and they distinguished it from a deposit; second, when a man takes it from him, and they distinguished it from a foundling. As for the luqta, there is no difference with us, and a luqta as he indicated by his saying: 'And the picking up of an animal is valid, and there is no difference between one place and another as he indicated by his saying.'
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from al-Walwaljiyya presents a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh between a luqta (lost property) and a laqit (foundling). The ruling is that if a finder of a luqta loses it and another person finds it, the first finder has no right to claim it from the second finder. This is because, unlike a deposit (wadi'a) where the depositor has a specific right, a luqta has no specific owner in appearance; anyone can pick it up with the intention of returning it. Therefore, the second finder's possession is equal to the first's. In contrast, for a foundling (laqit), the first person who picks him up becomes his custodian, and another person cannot take him away. The reason is that a foundling has no other apparent guardian, so the first finder's custody is established. The passage also addresses an objection: if the first finder has the right to own the luqta after announcing it (if he is poor), how can the second finder's taking it invalidate that? The answer is that the first finder's right to own is contingent upon completion of announcement, and if he loses it before that, his right is extinguished. The second finder's claim is equally valid. The passage concludes that the finder is not more entitled than another, and the ruling applies uniformly whether the luqta is lost or taken by another.

Key Terms
لقطة (luqta): Lost property found by someone else, with the obligation to announce and attempt to return to owner.
لقيط (laqit): A foundling (abandoned child) who is taken into care.
وديعة (wadi'a): A deposit held by a trustee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a finder of a luqta loses it and another person finds it, what is the ruling?
A) The first finder can claim it from the second finder.
B) There is no litigation between them because the second finder's position is like the first.
C) The first finder must be compensated by the second finder.
D) The second finder must give it to the first finder.

Key Takeaway
The first finder of a luqta loses all rights if it is lost and found by another; the second finder steps into the same position without any liability to the first.

Luqatah — Found Property

The Finder's Intention and the Condition of Witnesses
Explains intention, amana, and condition of witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the finder's liability based on his intention and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the finder's claim.

Core Idea
Intention determines amana or daman; the finder is liable if he takes for himself, but a dispute arises when he claims he took for the owner.

The fiqh of luqata (lost property) hinges on the finder's intention at the moment of picking up. If he intends to return it to the owner, the property becomes an amana (trust) in his hands, and he is not liable for loss unless negligent. But if he intends to keep it, he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and is liable. The Prophet's hadith commands the finder to recognize the item and announce it for a year, confirming the trust nature. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the finder's word when the owner denies his good intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key legal distinction
Understand that the finder's liability depends on his stated intention: if he admits taking for himself, he is liable by consensus; if both agree he took for owner, no liability. The dispute arises when the finder claims he took for owner but owner denies.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet said: 'Know its bag and its tie, then announce it for a year.' This shows the finder is entrusted (amana) to take care and announce, not to own. The hadith is a dalil for the ruling that the luqta is an amana.
Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the consensus cases
If the finder admits taking for himself, liability is ijma'. If both parties agree he took for owner, no liability. Witnesses (ishhad) are only a condition when there is a dispute.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: finder is liable (damin) because he took another's property and his claim of taking for owner is unproven. Abu Yusuf: not liable, his word is accepted because the apparent circumstance (dhahir) supports his virtue.
Both positions rely on dhahir arguments.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Yusuf's view, as recorded in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. This means in practice, if the finder claims he took for the owner and the owner denies, the finder is not liable.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

أقر أمانة (١) بين القلة ورجح القطة الحل والحرم إن أخذها ليردها على ربها وأشهد لإطلاق قوله عليه السلام اعرف عفاصها وكاءها ثم عرفها سنة وأما قوله عليه السلام في الحرم ولا تحل لقطته إلا لمنشدها» فتأويله أنه لا يحل الالتقاط إلا للتعريف والتخصيص بالحرم لبيان أنه لا يسقط التعريف فيه لمكان أنه للغرباء ظاهراً. وأما كونها أمانة فلأن الأخذ على هذا الوجه مأذون فيه شرعاً بل هو الأفضل عند العامة قيد بأخذها ليردها لأنه لو أقر أنه أخذها لنفسه يضمن بالإجماع لأنه أخذ مال الغير بغير إذنه وبغير إذن الشرع ولو تصادقا على أنه أخذها للمالك فلا ضمان إجماعاً لأن تصادقهما حجة في حقهما كالبينة وبه علم أن الإشهاد إنما هو شرط عند الاختلاف بأن قال الملتقط أخذته للمالك وكذبه المالك فإنه ضامن عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يضمن والقول قوله لأن الظاهر شاهد له لاختياره الحسبة دون المعصية. ولهما أنه الضمان بسبب وهو أخذ مال الغير وادعى ما يبرئه وهو الأخذ لمالكه وفيه وقع الشك فلا يبرأ. وما ذكر من الظاهر معارض بمثله لأن الظاهر أن يكون المتصرف عاملاً لنفسه . في الحاوي القدسي قول أبي يوسف قال وبه نأخذ .اهـ. ويكفيه في الإشهاد أن يقول من سمعتموه ينشد لقطة فدلوه علي واحدة كانت اللقطة أو أكثر لأنهم اسم جنس؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي الينابيع ذكر في بعض الكتب قول محمد مع أبي حنيفة والأصح أنه مع أبي يوسف اهـ. ويكفيه في الإشهاد أيضاً أن يقول عندي لقطة كما في شرح الطحاوي ولا يشترط التصريح بكونه لقطة لأنه لو قال عندي شيء فمن سمعتموه يسأل فدلوه على كفاه كما في الولوالجية. ومحل اشتراط الإشهاد عند الإمكان فلو لم يجد من يشهده عند الرفع أو خاف أنه لو أشهد عند الرفع يأخذه منه الظالم فترك الإشهاد لا يضمن؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي فتح القدير ؛ والقول قوله مع يمينه كوني منعني من الإشهاد كذا في الخانية. فإن وجد من يشهده فجاوزه ضمن وفي القنية وجد الصبي لقطة ولم يشهد يضمن كالبالغ اهـ. وهذا يدل على ما قدمناه من صحة التقاطه وفي الولوالجية محل الاختلاف فيما إذا اتفقا على كونها لقطة لكن اختلفا هلى التقطها للمالك أو لا، أما إذا اختلفا في كونها لقطة فقال صاحب المال أخذتها غصباً وقال الملتقط لقطة وقد أخذتها لك فالملتقط ضامن بالإجماع اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف حكم ما إذا ردها إلى مكانها.
He acknowledged it as an amana... [garbled]... the solution and the prohibition in the Haram: if he takes it to return it to its owner, and he witnesses, due to the absolute statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Know its bag and its tie, then announce it for a year.' As for his statement in the Haram: 'And its luqta is not permissible except for one who announces it,' its interpretation is that picking up is not permissible except for announcement, and specification of the Haram is to clarify that announcement is not waived there because it is apparently for strangers. As for it being an amana, because taking in this manner is permitted by Sharia, rather it is preferable in the view of the common people. He restricted it to taking it to return it, because if he admits that he took it for himself, he is liable by consensus, because he took the property of another without his permission and without permission of Sharia. And if they both agree that he took it for the owner, there is no liability by consensus, because their mutual agreement is binding on them like evidence. From this it is known that witnessing is only a condition in case of dispute. If the finder says 'I took it for the owner' and the owner denies him, then he is liable according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: He is not liable, and his word is accepted because outward circumstances are witness for him that he chose good deed over sin. They (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argued: Liability is due to the cause, which is taking possession of another's property, and he claims something that would discharge him, namely taking for its owner, and there is doubt, so he is not discharged. The outward circumstance they mention is countered by a similar one, because the outward circumstance is that a person acts for his own benefit. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi, it is the statement of Abu Yusuf, and he said: 'We take by it.' It suffices for witnessing that he says: 'Whoever you hear inquiring about a luqta, then direct him to me,' whether the luqta is one or more, because they are a common noun; as in al-Hidaya. In al-Yanabi', it is mentioned in some books that Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa, but the most correct is that he agrees with Abu Yusuf. It also suffices for witnessing that he says: 'I have a luqta,' as in Sharh al-Tahawi, and it is not required to explicitly say it is a luqta, because if he says 'I have something,' then whoever you hear asking, then direct him to me, it suffices, as in al-Walwaljiyya. The condition of requiring witnessing is when it is possible. So if he does not find someone to witness at the time of picking up, or he fears that if he witnesses at the time of picking up, a tyrant will take it from him, then if he leaves out witnessing, he is not liable; as in al-Khaniya. In Fath al-Qadir: 'His word with his oath is accepted that he was prevented from witnessing,' as in al-Khaniya. If he finds someone to witness and he bypasses him, he is liable. In al-Qunyah: A child found a luqta and did not witness, he is liable like an adult. This indicates what we have stated about the validity of his picking up. In al-Walwaljiyya, the place of disagreement is when they both agree that it is a luqta, but differ on whether he picked it up for the owner or not. As for when they differ on whether it is a luqta, for example the owner says 'You took it as usurpation' and the finder says 'It is a luqta and I took it for you,' then the finder is liable by consensus. The author did not mention the ruling if he returns it to its place.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh regarding the finder's intention when picking up lost property. The finder's liability depends on his stated intention. If he admits he took it for himself, he becomes a guarantor (damin) by consensus. If both parties agree he took it for the owner, there is no liability. The dispute arises when the finder claims he took it for the owner but the owner denies. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the finder is liable because he took someone else's property and his claim to have taken it for the owner is unsubstantiated. Abu Yusuf, however, says the finder is not liable and his word is accepted because the apparent circumstance (dhahir) supports him: his act is one of virtue (hissa) rather than sin. The text notes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Yusuf, as recorded in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. The passage also explains the condition of witnesses (ishhad). Witnesses are required only when there is a dispute. If the finder can produce witnesses at the time of picking up or fears a tyrant, he may omit witnessing without liability. The specific wording of witnessing is flexible; saying 'I have a luqta' or 'I have something' and directing inquirers suffices. The passage also addresses the ruling for luqta in the Haram (Mecca): picking up is permissible only for the purpose of announcement, drawing from the hadith 'Its luqta is not permissible except for one who announces it.'

Key Terms
أمانة (amana): A trust; the luqta becomes an amana in the hands of the finder if he takes it with the intention to return it.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; the finder becomes a guarantor responsible for compensation if he takes it for himself or fails to prove he took it for the owner.
إشهاد (ishhad): The act of taking witnesses to testify that the finder picked up the luqta for the purpose of returning it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Abu Yusuf when the finder claims he took the luqta for the owner but the owner denies?
A) The finder is liable.
B) The finder is not liable and his word is accepted.
C) The finder is liable only if he is rich.
D) The finder must return the luqta to the owner immediately.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the finder's intention at the time of picking up lost property determines liability; if he intends to return it, the property becomes an amana, and the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that his word is accepted in case of dispute even without witnesses, provided he could not obtain them.

Luqatah — Found Property
intermediate
8 min
Luqatah: Liability and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Finder's Word
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability in luqatah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for picking up lost property (luqatah), identify when the finder becomes liable for compensation (daman), and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the finder's claim in case of owner's denial.

Core Idea
The finder is a trustee; liability arises only if he takes for himself or fails to make witnesses when possible.

Lost property (luqatah) is a common occurrence, and the Shari'a has detailed rules to protect both the finder and the owner. The Hanafi school distinguishes between picking up with intention to return (a trust) and picking up for oneself (usurpation). A key point of internal difference is whether the finder's word is accepted when the owner disputes his intention. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the conditions that affect liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
First, recognize that picking up luqatah for the purpose of returning it to the owner is permissible and recommended; it becomes obligatory if the item is at risk. The finder holds it as a trust (amanah).
2
Determine when liability attaches
The finder is liable if he admits taking it for himself, or if he fails to make witnesses (ishhad) when possible. Without ishhad, his claim of taking for the owner becomes disputed.
Ishhad is a condition only in case of dispute according to the text.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the finder's word
When the owner denies the finder's claim of taking for the owner, the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold the finder liable, while Abu Yusuf does not. Understand the arguments: cause of liability vs. apparent piety.
The mufta bihi is the opinion of Abu Yusuf.
4
Examine the conditions for ishhad and ta'rif
Witnessing at the time of picking up is required; if not possible, the finder is excused. Announcing (ta'rif) is also required, and its duration is not fixed (according to the preferred view).
The passage discusses that some scholars consider ishhad at time of taking sufficient for ta'rif.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider cases like returning the item to its place after moving, riding a found animal, or a boy finding a lost item. Each scenario triggers liability or absolution based on the rules.
The detail of returning to place before moving absolves; after moving, liable.

حنيفة والأصح أنه مع أبي يوسف اهـ. ويكفيه في الإشهاد أيضاً أن يقول عندي لقطة كما في شرح الطحاوي ولا يشترط التصريح بكونه لقطة لأنه لو قال عندي شيء فمن سمعتموه يسأل فدلوه على كفاه كما في الولوالجية. ومحل اختلفا هلى التقطها للمالك أو لا، أما إذا اختلفا في كونها لقطة فقال صاحب المال أخذتها غصباً وقال الملتقط لقطة وقد أخذتها لك فالملتقط ضامن بالإجماع اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف حكم ما إذا ردها إلى مكانها. وفي الولوالجية وغيرها وإذا أخذ الرجل ليعرفها ثم أعادها في المكان الذي أخذها منه فقد برئ عن الضمان. هذا إذا أعادها قبل أن يتحول عن ذلك المكان، أما إذا أعادها بعد ما تحول يضمن. ولو كانت دابة فركبها ثم نزل عنها فتركها في مكانها على قول أبي يوسف هو ضامن وعلى قول زفر لا، وكذا إذا أخذ الخاتم من أصبع نائم ثم أعاده إلى أصبعه بعدما انتبه ولو أعاده قبل أن ينتبه برئ اتفاقاً .اهـ. والتفصيل المذكور خلاف ظاهر الرواية فإنها عدم الضمان مطلقاً كما وهو في فتح القدير ورجحه في البدائع أيضاً. وأطلق في الإشهاد فانصرف إلى من تقبل شهادته عدلان ولذا قال في فتح القدير : وظاهر المبسوط اشتراط عدلين اهـ . وهو قوله : (وعرف إلى أن علم أن ربها لا يطلبها معطوف على «أشهد» فظاهره أن التعريف شرط أيضاً وأن الإشهاد لا يكفي لنفي الضمان وهكذا شرط في المحيط لنفي الضمان الإشهاد وإشاعة التعريف. وحكى في الظهيرية فيه اختلافاً فقال قال الحلواني : أدنى ما يكون من التعريف أن يشهد عند الأخذ ويقول آخذها لا ردها فإن فعل ذلك ثم لم يعرفها بعد ذلك كفى. ومن المشايخ من قال : يأتي على أبواب المساجد وينادي اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: وعلى هذا لا يلزم الإشهاد أي التعريف وقت الأخذ بل لا بد منه قبل هلاكها ليعرف أنه أخذها ليردها لا لنفسه اهـ. وهو غير صحيح لأن الإشهاد لا بد منه على قول الإمام عند الأخذ باتفاق المشايخ، وإنما اختلفوا هل يكفي هذا الإشهاد عند الأخذ عن التعريف بعده أو لا، ولم يقل أحد إن التعريف بعد الأخذ يكفي عن الإشهاد وقت الأخذ فليتأمل. ولم يجعل للتعريف مدة اتباعاً لشمس الأئمة السرخسي فإنه بنى الحكم على غالب الرأي فيعرف القليل والكثير إلى أن يغلب على رأيه أن صاحبه لا يطلبه بعد ذلك. وصححه في الهداية وقال في البزازية والجوهرة. وعليه الفتوى وهو خلاف ظاهر الرواية فإنه التقدير بالحول في القليل والكثير كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وفي الظهيرية ثم على قول من قدر بحول اختلف فيه؛ قيل يعرفها كل جمعة، وقيل كل شهر، وقيل كل ستة أشهر . قال السرخسي : حكي أن بعض العلماء ببلخ وجد لقطة وكان محتاجاً إليها وقد قال في نفسه لا بد من تعريفها ولو عرفتها في المصر ربما يظهر صاحبها فخرج من المصر حتى انتهى إلى رأس بئر فدلى رأسه في البئر وجعل يقول وجدت كذا، فمن سمعتموه ينشد ذلك فدلوه علي وبجنب البئر رجل برقع شملته وكان صاحب اللقطة فتعلق به حتى أخذها منه ليعلم أن المقدور كائن لا محالة، فلا ينبغي له أن يترك ما لزمه شرعاً وهو إظهار التعريف قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يكثر همك ما يقدر يكون وما ترزق يأتيك» اهـ. وهو خطأ هذا الملتقط لأن هذا ليس بتعريف اتفاقاً. قال في الجوهرة : من ثم التعريف إنما يكون جهراً في الأسواق وفي أبواب المساجد وفي الموضع الذي وجدها فيه. وفي الجامع : وإن كانت شيئاً لا يبقى عرفه حتى يخاف فساده فيتصدق به اهـ ؛ كذا الهداية. وإن وجد اللقطة رجلان عرفاها جميعاً واشتركا في حكمها اهـ. وقدمنا أن الملتقط إذا
Book of Lost and Found. For we say: We have explained that they are two issues: first, regarding when it is lost and they distinguished between it and the deposit; second, regarding when a man takes it from him and they distinguished between it and the foundling. As for luqatah, there is no distinction according to us. And luqatah, as indicated by his statement, 'And his picking up the animal is valid,' and no distinction between one place and another as indicated by his statement, 'He acknowledged it as a trust.' And he preferred luqatah in the Halal and the Haram if he takes it to return it to its owner and he makes witnesses, due to the general meaning of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Know its string and its bag, then announce it for a year.' As for his statement (peace be upon him) regarding the Haram: 'And its luqatah is not permissible except for the one who announces it,' its interpretation is that picking up is not permissible except for announcement, and the specification for the Haram is to clarify that announcement is not dropped there because it is apparently for strangers. As for it being a trust, it is because taking in this manner is legally permitted; rather, it is preferable for the general public, restricted by taking it to return it because if he acknowledges that he took it for himself, he is liable by consensus, because he took another's property without his permission and without legal permission. If they both confirm that he took it for the owner, there is no liability by consensus because their mutual confirmation is a proof regarding them like evidence. And by this it is known that witnessing is only a condition in case of dispute: if the finder says 'I took it for the owner' and the owner denies him, then he is liable according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: He is not liable, and the say is his word because the apparent circumstance witnesses for him due to his choosing piety over disobedience. For the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is that liability is due to the cause—taking another's property—and he claimed something that would absolve him, namely taking for its owner, and doubt occurs therein, so he is not absolved. And what was mentioned regarding apparent circumstance is countered by a similar one because the apparent is that the acting person acts for himself. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi, the statement of Abu Yusuf is 'and we take with it' end. And it suffices for witnessing that he say 'Whoever among you hears someone announcing a lost item, direct him to me,' whether the item is one or more because they are a common noun; thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Yanabi', it is mentioned in some books that Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa, and the correct is that he is with Abu Yusuf end. And it also suffices for witnessing that he say 'I have a lost item' as in Sharh al-Tahawi, and explicit mention that it is a lost item is not required because if he says 'I have something, whoever among you hears someone asking, direct him to me,' it suffices as in al-Walwaljiyya. And the condition of witnessing is applicable when possible; if he cannot find anyone to witness when picking up, or fears that if he witnesses when picking up the oppressor would take it from him, so he abandons witnessing, he is not liable; thus in al-Khaniyya. And in Fath al-Qadir: And the say is his word with his oath: 'What prevented me from witnessing is such'—thus in al-Khaniyya. If he finds someone to witness and passes it up, he is liable. And in al-Qunyah: A boy found a lost item and did not witness—he is liable like an adult end. And this indicates what we have mentioned regarding the validity of his picking up. And in al-Walwaljiyya, the point of contention is when they agree that it is a lost item but differ on whether he picked it up for the owner or not. As for when they differ on whether it is a lost item, the owner says 'you took it as a usurpation' and the finder says 'it is a lost item and I took it for you,' then the finder is liable by consensus end. And the author did not mention the ruling on returning it to its place. And in al-Walwaljiyya and others: If a man takes it to announce it then returns it to the place he took it from, he is absolved from liability. This is if he returns it before moving from that place; if he returns it after moving, he is liable. And if it was an animal, he rode it then dismounted and left it in its place—according to Abu Yusuf he is liable, and according to Zufar, no. Similarly, if he took a ring from a sleeping person's finger then returned it to his finger after he woke up; if he returns it before he wakes up, he is absolved by agreement end. And the mentioned detail is contrary to the apparent narration, which is no liability absolutely, as it is in Fath al-Qadir and he preferred it in al-Bada'i as well. And he gave absolute scope in witnessing, so it is understood to refer to those whose testimony is accepted—two just witnesses. Hence, he said in Fath al-Qadir: 'And the apparent of al-Mabsut is the condition of two just witnesses end.' And his statement 'And announce until you know that its owner does not seek it' is conjoined to 'he witnesses,' so its apparent is that announcement is also a condition and that witnessing alone does not suffice to negate liability. Thus it is conditioned in al-Muhit to negate liability: witnessing and spreading announcement. And in al-Dhahiriyyah, difference is narrated therein, so al-Halwani said: The minimum of announcement is that he witnesses at the time of taking and says 'I take it to return it'; if he does that and then does not announce it afterwards, it suffices. Some shaykhs said: He goes to the doors of the mosques and calls out end. And in Fath al-Qadir: According to this, witnessing (i.e., announcement) at the time of taking is not required; rather, it must be done before its destruction so that it is known that he took it to return it, not for himself end. And this is incorrect because witnessing is necessary according to the Imam at the time of taking by agreement of the shaykhs; they only differed on whether this witnessing at the time of taking suffices from announcement afterwards or not. And no one said that announcement after taking suffices from witnessing at the time of taking, so one should reflect. And he did not set a time limit for announcement, following Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, for he based the ruling on the predominant opinion; so he announces a little or much until it becomes predominantly his opinion that its owner will not seek it afterwards. And he corrected it in al-Hidayah and said in al-Bazzaziyya and al-Jawharah: And on it is the fatwa, and it is contrary to the apparent narration, which is the estimation of one year for little and much as al-Usbijabi mentioned. And in al-Dhahiriyyah: Then, according to those who estimated a year, there is difference: it is said he announces every Friday, every month, every six months. Al-Sarakhsi said: It is narrated that some scholars in Balkh found a lost item and were in need of it, and he said to himself: 'I must announce it; if I announce it in the city, perhaps its owner will appear.' So he left the city until he reached the mouth of a well, put his head into the well, and began to say: 'I found such and such; whoever among you hears someone announcing that, direct him to me.' And beside the well was a man who had lost his cloak, and he was the owner of the lost item; he clung to him until he took it from him. This is to teach that what is predestined will inevitably happen, so one should not abandon what is obligatory upon him legally, which is manifesting announcement. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not worry excessively about what is predestined; what is destined will come to you.' End. And this finder was wrong because this is not an announcement by agreement. He said in al-Jawharah: Hence, announcement is only aloud in the markets, at the doors of mosques, and in the place where he found it. And in al-Jami': If it is something that does not last, he announces it until he fears its spoilage, then he gives it in charity end; thus in al-Hidayah. And if two men find the lost item, they both announce it and share in its ruling end. And we have mentioned that the finder, if...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq dealing with the laws of luqatah (lost property). The author begins by clarifying the distinction between different types of lost items: if property is lost by the owner himself versus if someone takes it from him, and between a found animal and a found child. He affirms that for luqatah (a lost item that is not an animal or child), there is no distinction in ruling between the Haram (Mecca) and other places, as long as the finder takes it with the intention to return it to its owner and makes witnesses (ishhad). This is based on the hadith: 'Know its string and its bag, then announce it for a year.' The hadith about the Haram ('its luqatah is not permissible except for the one who announces it') is interpreted to mean that picking up is only permissible for the purpose of announcement, and the specification of the Haram is to emphasize that announcement is not dropped there because strangers frequent it. The finder holds the item as a trust (amanah) because the taking is legally permitted; indeed, it is preferable for the layperson. The author then discusses the issue of guarantee (daman). If the finder admits that he took it for himself, he is liable by consensus because he took another's property without permission. If both parties agree that the finder took it for the owner, there is no liability. Witnessing is a condition only in case of dispute. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), if the finder claims he took it for the owner and the owner denies, the finder is liable. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the finder is not liable and his word is accepted because the apparent circumstance supports him—he chose piety over disobedience. The author notes that in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, the fatwa is taken with Abu Yusuf. However, in some books, Muhammad is said to be with Abu Hanifa, but the correct view is that he is with Abu Yusuf. The discussion continues on what suffices for witnessing: saying 'whoever hears someone announcing a lost item, direct him to me' is sufficient, and explicit mention of 'luqata' is not required. The condition of witnessing is applicable only when possible; if the finder cannot find witnesses or fears an oppressor, he may omit it without liability. If he could find witnesses and does not, he is liable. The passage then covers the ruling on returning the item to its original place. If the finder takes it for announcement and then returns it to the same place before moving from that spot, he is absolved of liability. If he moves and then returns, he remains liable. There is a difference regarding riding a found animal: according to Abu Yusuf, riding it then leaving it in place makes him liable; Zufar disagrees. Similarly for a ring taken from a sleeping person. The author notes that this detailed ruling is contrary to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), which holds no liability absolutely, and this latter view is preferred in Fath al-Qadir and al-Bada'i. The passage then addresses the requirement of announcement (ta'rif). The text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq says 'and announce until you know that its owner does not seek it.' This is conjoined to 'he witnesses,' showing that announcement is also a condition for negating liability. There is a difference of opinion on the minimum announcement: al-Halwani said that witnessing at the time of taking and stating the intention to return suffices, even without subsequent announcement. Others require announcement at mosque doors. The author criticizes Fath al-Qadir's claim that witnessing at the time of taking is not necessary; he asserts that according to all shaykhs, witnessing at the time of taking is necessary on the Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) view; the dispute is only on whether that witnessing suffices for subsequent announcement. Regarding the duration of announcement, al-Sarakhsi holds that there is no fixed time; the finder announces until he is predominantly of the opinion that the owner will not seek it. This is the view adopted in al-Hidayah, al-Bazzaziyya, and al-Jawharah, and the fatwa is upon it, though it contradicts the apparent narration which prescribes one year. The passage ends with a cautionary tale about a scholar who attempted a faulty announcement and was corrected, emphasizing that announcement must be public in markets and mosque doors, not in hiding. If the item is perishable, the finder announces until spoilage is feared, then gives it in charity. If two people find the item, they both announce and share the ruling.

Key Terms
اللقطة (al-luqatah): Lost property that is not an animal or a child; typically movable wealth found by someone. The term is also used generally for all found items.
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): Having witnesses present at the time of picking up the lost item to attest that the finder took it with the intention to return it to its owner. It is a condition to avoid liability in case of dispute.
التعريف (al-ta'rif): Announcement of the lost item to the public in places like markets and mosque doors, so that the owner may claim it. It is a duty on the finder.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability to compensate the owner for the lost item if it is lost or damaged due to the finder's fault or if the finder fails to follow proper procedures. The finder is a trustee (amin) unless he exceeds limits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), if the finder and owner dispute whether the finder took the item for the owner, who is favored?
A) The owner, because property rights are established.
B) The finder, because the apparent circumstance supports his piety.
C) Neither, the case is judged based on evidence.
D) The finder only if he has witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The finder of lost property is not liable if he takes it with intention to return and makes witnesses when possible; in a dispute, the relied-upon Hanafi position favors the finder's claim with an oath.

Returning Found Items to Original Place: Liability and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on finder's liability after returning item to exact spot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a finder returns a lost item to its original location, distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Zufar from the Zahir al-Riwaya, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Returning a lost item to the exact spot before moving exonerates; after moving, liability attaches—but Zahir al-Riwaya holds no liability ever.

The fiqh of luqatah (found property) is not just about announcing the find; it also governs when the finder's responsibility ends. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reveals a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: does returning the item to its original place always free the finder from liability, or are there conditions? Prepare to navigate the reasoning of the Sahibayn against the authoritative Zahir al-Riwaya.

Guided Path
1
State the Zahir al-Riwaya position
Articulate the transmitted ruling from Imam Muhammad: a finder who returns the item to the exact place is free from liability absolutely, regardless of moving or using.
This is the default ruling in the six major books.
2
Identify the opposing detail
Note the conditions introduced by Abu Yusuf and Zufar: (a) moving away before return triggers liability (both agree); (b) using the item (e.g., riding animal, removing ring after waking) triggers liability for Abu Yusuf but not for Zufar.
The disagreement between the two Sahibayn is also part of the detail.
3
Analyse the reasoning
Understand the legal basis: Abu Yusuf views moving or using as changing the finder's status from trustee (amin) to usurper (ghasib), while Zufar considers that returning to the same spot restores the original state even after use.
The ring case illustrates that the owner's state (asleep vs awake) matters in the detailed view.
4
Apply the tarjih
Observe that later authorities (Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir, al-Bada'i') prefer the Zahir al-Riwaya because it is the most reliably transmitted, considering the detailed views as nawadir.
Tarjih is based on authority weight (zahir al-riwaya vs. nawadir).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in fatwa, a finder who returns the item to the exact spot is not liable even if he moved or used it, providing ease and avoiding strict liability.
This is an application of the Hanafi maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعادها في المكان الذي أخذها منه فقد برئ عن الضمان. هذا إذا أعادها قبل أن يتحول عن ذلك المكان، أما إذا أعادها بعد ما تحول يضمن. ولو كانت دابة فركبها ثم نزل عنها فتركها في مكانها على قول أبي يوسف هو ضامن وعلى قول زفر لا، وكذا إذا أخذ الخاتم من أصبع نائم ثم أعاده إلى أصبعه بعدما انتبه من تلك النومة ولو أعاده قبل أن ينتبه من اتفاقاً .اهـ. والتفصيل المذكور خلاف ظاهر الرواية فإنها عدم الضمان مطلقاً الوجه كما وهو في فتح القدير ورجحه في البدائع أيضاً.
He returned it to the place from which he took it, then he is free from liability. This is if he returned it before he moved from that place. As for if he returned it after he moved, he is liable. If it was a riding animal, and he rode it, then dismounted and left it in its place, according to Abu Yusuf he is liable, and according to Zufar no. Similarly, if he took a ring from the finger of a sleeping person, then returned it to his finger after he woke from that sleep; if he returned it before he woke, then (liability is dropped) by agreement. End quote. The detail mentioned is contrary to the Zahir al-Riwaya, which is no liability absolutely, as is the position in Fath al-Qadir and preferred in al-Bada'i' as well.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the liability of a finder who returns a lost item to its original location. The main ruling states that if the finder returns the item to the exact place from which he took it, before leaving that location, he is free from liability. If he returns it after moving away, he is liable. The text then presents two specific cases: a riding animal and a ring from a sleeping person. In the case of the animal, Abu Yusuf holds the finder liable if he rides it and then leaves it, because riding constitutes use and moving. Zufar holds that returning it to the same place after riding does not incur liability because the return suffices. The ring case is similar: if the finder returns the ring to the sleeping person's finger after they wake, the finder is liable; if before waking, liability is dropped by agreement. The commentator notes that this detailed ruling contradicts the Zahir al-Riwaya (the transmitted position from Imam Muhammad), which holds no liability in all cases. The preferred position in Fath al-Qadir and al-Bada'i' is the one from Zahir al-Riwaya.

Key Terms
الضمان (al-daman): Liability to compensate the owner if the item is lost or damaged.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad in the six core books, considered the authoritative position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a finder takes a lost item, moves to another city, then returns to the original spot and puts the item back, what is the ruling according to the detailed view in the passage?
A) He is free from liability.
B) He is liable.
C) He is liable only if he used the item.
D) He is free if he returns within a year.

Key Takeaway
A finder who returns a lost item to its exact original place is free from liability per the authoritative Zahir al-Riwaya, regardless of moving or using the item.

Condition for Ishhad in Luqatah: Two Just Witnesses
Ruling statement on condition of ishhad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required number and quality of witnesses for ishhad in luqatah and explain its consequence for the finder's liability.

Core Idea
Ishhad requires two just male witnesses to exempt the finder from liability.

In the chapter of luqatah, a crucial condition for the finder to avoid liability if the lost item is later lost or damaged is the act of ishhad — taking witnesses that he picked it up with the intention to return it. This passage clarifies that the witnesses must be two just males ('adlan). This ruling is drawn from earlier Hanafi authorities and ensures that the claim of finding is established with reliable testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'ishhad' in the context of luqatah. It is a required condition for the finder to be exempt from liability.
2
Identify the condition
The condition is that the witnesses must be two just males ('adlan). The text emphasizes this by referring to Fath al-Qadir and al-Mabsut.
3
Understand the consequence
If ishhad is performed with two just witnesses, the finder is not liable if the item is lost. If this condition is not met, the finder remains liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في الإشهاد فانصرف إلى من تقبل شهادته عدلان ولذا قال في فتح القدير : وظاهر المبسوط اشتراط عدلين اهـ .
And he made an absolute statement concerning testimony, so it refers to those whose testimony is accepted: two just witnesses. For this reason, he said in Fath al-Qadir: 'The apparent meaning of al-Mabsut is the requirement of two just witnesses.' End quote.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This is a ruling statement clarifying that the requirement of 'ishhad' (taking witnesses) in the context of luqatah (finding lost property) must be fulfilled by two just witnesses ('adlan). The commentator notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq spoke in absolute terms about ishhad, which implies it refers to the standard witnesses whose testimony is accepted in Islamic courts. In Fath al-Qadir, this is supported by referring to al-Mabsut, which explicitly requires two just witnesses. This means that if a finder wants to exonerate himself from liability through testimony, he must have two upright witnesses testify to his taking of the item for return.

Key Terms
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): Taking witnesses to the fact of picking up the lost item with intention to return it.
عدلان (adlan): Two male witnesses who are upright (adil) in character.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One male witness who is just.
B) Two witnesses, male or female, who are just.
C) Two just male witnesses.
D) Two witnesses regardless of their justice.

Key Takeaway
Ishhad in luqatah requires two just male witnesses to exempt the finder from liability.

Announcement (Ta'rif) for Found Items: Conditions and Duration
Dispute over necessity and duration of public announcement for found items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ishhad and ta'rif in luqatah, state the relied-upon Hanafi view on the duration of ta'rif, and apply the ruling to a real scenario.

Core Idea
Taking witnesses at the time of finding does not replace the obligation of public announcement — both are wajib.

The finder of a lost item must both take witnesses (ishhad) and publicly announce (ta'rif) to avoid liability. This passage explores disagreements among Hanafi scholars on whether ishhad alone is sufficient, and how long ta'rif must continue. Understanding these conditions is essential for any practitioner dealing with lost property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
From the phrase 'he took witnesses and announce,' note that both ishhad and ta'rif are presented as conditions. Determine the legal status of each.
The author's phrasing implies they are separate obligations.
2
Analyze the first dispute: ishhad vs. ta'rif
Al-Halwani held that ishhad at the time of taking suffices to negate liability. Others required actual public announcement. Examine the arguments and the Hanafi response.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the second dispute: duration of ta'rif
Zahir al-Riwaya sets one year for all items. Al-Sarakhsi and al-Hidayah adopted the view of announcing until the finder is confident the owner will not seek it. Compare the two views.
The mufta bihi follows Sarakhsi's view.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a factual scenario, identify whether both conditions were met and whether the duration was sufficient. State the hukm.
Use the story of the scholar in Balkh as a negative example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وعرف إلى أن علم أن ربها لا يطلبها معطوف على «أشهد» فظاهره أن التعريف شرط أيضاً وأن الإشهاد لا يكفي لنفي الضمان وهكذا شرط في المحيط لنفي الضمان الإشهاد وإشاعة التعريف. وحكى في الظهيرية فيه اختلافاً فقال قال الحلواني : أدنى ما يكون من التعريف أن يشهد عند الأخذ ويقول آخذها لا ردها فإن فعل ذلك ثم لم يعرفها بعد ذلك كفى. ومن المشايخ من قال : يأتي على أبواب المساجد وينادي اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: وعلى هذا لا يلزم الإشهاد أي التعريف وقت الأخذ بل لا بد منه قبل هلاكها ليعرف أنه أخذها ليردها لا لنفسه اهـ. وهو غير صحيح لأن الإشهاد لا بد منه على قول الإمام عند الأخذ باتفاق المشايخ، وإنما اختلفوا هل يكفي هذا الإشهاد عند الأخذ عن التعريف بعده أو لا، ولم يقل أحد إن التعريف بعد الأخذ يكفي عن الإشهاد وقت الأخذ فليتأمل. ولم يجعل للتعريف مدة اتباعاً لشمس الأئمة السرخسي فإنه بنى الحكم على غالب الرأي فيعرف القليل والكثير إلى أن يغلب على رأيه أن صاحبه لا يطلبه بعد ذلك. وصححه في الهداية وقال في البزازية والجوهرة. وعليه الفتوى وهو خلاف ظاهر الرواية فإنه التقدير بالحول في القليل والكثير كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وفي الظهيرية ثم على قول من قدر بحول اختلف فيه؛ قيل يعرفها كل جمعة، وقيل كل شهر، وقيل كل ستة أشهر . قال السرخسي : حكي أن بعض العلماء ببلخ وجد لقطة وكان محتاجاً إليها وقد قال في نفسه لا بد من تعريفها ولو عرفتها في المصر ربما يظهر صاحبها فخرج من المصر حتى انتهى إلى رأس بئر فدلى رأسه في البئر وجعل يقول وجدت كذا، فمن سمعتموه ينشد ذلك فدلوه علي وبجنب البئر رجل برقع شملته وكان صاحب اللقطة فتعلق به حتى أخذها منه ليعلم أن المقدور كائن لا محالة، فلا ينبغي له أن يترك ما لزمه شرعاً وهو إظهار التعريف قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يكثر همك ما يقدر يكون وما ترزق يأتيك» اهـ. وهو خطأ هذا الملتقط لأن هذا ليس بتعريف اتفاقاً. قال في الجوهرة : من ثم التعريف إنما يكون جهراً في الأسواق وفي أبواب المساجد وفي الموضع الذي وجدها فيه. وفي الجامع : وإن كانت شيئاً لا يبقى عرفه حتى يخاف فساده فيتصدق به اهـ؛ كذا الهداية.
His statement: 'And announce until he knows that its owner does not seek it' is coordinated with 'he took witnesses.' So its apparent meaning is that announcement is also a condition, and that taking witnesses is not sufficient to negate liability. Thus in al-Muhit it is stipulated for negating liability: taking witnesses and spreading the announcement. In al-Zuhayriyya it is reported that there is disagreement about it. Al-Halwani said: The minimum of announcement is that he takes witnesses at the time of taking and says: I take it to return it. If he does that and then does not announce it afterwards, it suffices. Some shaykhs said: He should go to the doors of mosques and call out. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: According to this, taking witnesses (i.e., announcement) is not necessary at the time of taking, but it is necessary before it perishes so that it is known that he took it to return it, not for himself. End quote. But this is incorrect because taking witnesses at the time of taking is necessary according to the Imam, by agreement of the shaykhs. They only disagreed about whether this taking witnesses at the time suffices for the announcement afterwards or not. No one said that announcement after taking suffices for taking witnesses at the time of taking, so reflect. He did not set a time for announcement, following Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, who built the ruling on predominant opinion. So he announces a little and a lot until it becomes predominant in his opinion that its owner will not seek it afterwards. This was endorsed in al-Hidayah, and stated in al-Bazzaziyya and al-Jawhara, and upon it is the fatwa. It is contrary to Zahir al-Riwaya, which is the estimation of a year for little and much, as mentioned by al-Usbijabi. In al-Zuhayriyya: then according to those who estimate a year, they disagreed: some said he announces every Friday, some said every month, some said every six months. Al-Sarakhsi said: It is narrated that one of the scholars in Balkh found a lost item and was in need of it. He said to himself: I must announce it. But if I announce it in the city, perhaps its owner will appear. So he went out of the city until he reached the mouth of a well, put his head into the well, and started saying: 'I found such and such; whoever hears this announcement, point me out to him.' Beside the well was a man wearing a cloak; he was the owner of the lost item. He grabbed him and took the item from him. So that it be known that the destined is inevitable, one should not abandon what is legally required, which is making the announcement. The Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Do not let your worry be excessive; what is destined will happen, and your sustenance will come to you.' End quote. This finder was wrong because this is not announcement by agreement. In al-Jawhara: For this reason, announcement is only to be done aloud in the marketplaces, at the doors of mosques, and in the place where he found it. In al-Jami': If it is something that does not last, he announces until he fears its corruption, then he gives charity with it. End quote. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion about the conditions and duration of ta'rif (public announcement) for found items. The commentary begins by explaining that the text 'and announce until he knows that its owner does not seek it' is coordinated with 'he took witnesses,' implying that both ishhad and ta'rif are necessary conditions to negate liability. The commentator notes that al-Halwani held that simply taking witnesses at the time of picking up and stating the intention is sufficient, while other shaykhs required actual calling out at mosque doors. A dispute is then reported about whether ishhad at the time of taking suffices for the entire announcement requirement. The correct view, according to the commentator, is that ishhad is essential at the time of taking, and announcement must also be done. Regarding the duration, al-Sarakhsi adopted the view that the finder should announce until he is confident that the owner will not seek it, regardless of time. This was endorsed in al-Hidayah and is the relied-upon fatwa, though it contradicts the Zahir al-Riwaya which fixes the period at one year. For those who hold the one-year view, there is disagreement about frequency (weekly, monthly, etc.). The story of the scholar in Balkh illustrates a failed attempt to avoid proper announcement; the finder tried to announce in a well to avoid detection, but the owner was nearby. The lesson is that announcement must be genuine and public. The passage concludes by specifying that announcement should be aloud in markets and mosques, and if the item is perishable, the finder should give it in charity after announcing enough.

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rif): Public announcement of the found item to locate its owner.
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): Taking witnesses at the time of picking up the item to confirm the finder's intention to return it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in al-Hidayah, how long should a finder announce a lost item?
A) One year exactly
B) Until he fears it will perish
C) Until he is confident the owner will not seek it
D) Until the owner appears

Key Takeaway
For found items, the finder must both take witnesses and publicly announce until confident the owner will not return.

Two Finders: Joint Responsibility in Luqatah
Ruling statement on joint finders.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when two people find a lost item and identify their joint obligations.

Core Idea
Two finders share the duty to announce and all subsequent rulings of luqatah.

When two people find a lost item together, the Hanafi fiqh assigns them joint responsibility. This lesson explains the rule from the passage, ensuring clarity in their obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognise that two people have found a lost item simultaneously. This is the trigger for the joint ruling.
2
State the ruling
Both must announce the find together. They share the same duties as a single finder: announcement for one year, then choosing to keep, give charity, or give to the child (if applicable).
The text says they 'share in its ruling' – meaning all subsequent luqatah rules apply jointly.
3
Understand joint nature
Neither can act independently; consent of both is needed for decisions about the item.
This prevents disputes and protects the owner's rights.
4
Apply to practice
In real life, both finders must agree on the announcement method and subsequent disposal. If they disagree, a judge may decide.
This is derived from general luqatah principles, though not explicit in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن وجد اللقطة رجلان عرفاها جميعاً واشتركا في حكمها اهـ. وقدمنا أن الملتقط إذا كان صبياً عرفها وليه - زاد في القنية - أو وصيه ثم له أن يتصدق بها. وسكت عن حكم تمليكها للصبي لو كان فقيراً لأنه يعلم بالأولى، وينبغي أن لا تجوز الصدقة بها من وليه أو وصيه لما في ذلك من الإضرار على احتمال أن لا يجيز مالكها إذا حضر والعين هالكة من يد الفقير فإنه يضمنها من مال الصبي وليس في إمساكها أو تمليكها ضرر. ثم رأيت بعد ذلك في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان للمصنف أنه قال : ينبغي على قول أصحابنا إذا تصدق بها الأب أو الوصي ثم ظهر صاحب اللقطة وضمنها أن يكون الضمان في مالهما دون الصبي اهـ. هذا البحث فلا إشكال في جواز تصدقهما حينئذ
And if two men find a lost item, they both announce it and share its ruling. End quote. And we have mentioned that if the finder is a child, his guardian announces it – added in al-Qiniyya – or his executor, then he may give it in charity. He remained silent about the ruling of giving it to the child (as owner) if he is poor, because it is known a fortiori. It is not appropriate for the guardian or executor to give it in charity because of the harm involved if the owner does not ratify it when he appears and the item is wasted from the hand of the poor person, for then the guardian would guarantee it from the child's wealth, whereas there is no harm in keeping it or giving it to the child. Then after that I saw in the commentary on Ibn Wahban's poem by the author that he said: According to our companions, if the father or executor gives it in charity and then the owner appears and claims compensation, the guarantee is upon them (the father/executor) and not upon the child. End quote. This discussion removes any problem about the permissibility of their giving charity in that case.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios: two finders and a child finder. If two people find a lost item together, they both must announce it, and they share the same rulings as a single finder. For a child finder, the child's legal guardian (father or executor) performs the announcement on his behalf. After proper announcement, the guardian may give the item in charity if the owner is not found, but there is a nuance: if the child is poor, arguably it would be better to give the item to the child rather than charity, because charity to a stranger might cause loss if the owner later claims compensation – in that case the guardian would be liable for the value from the child's own wealth. However, the commentator cites a later source (Sharh Manzumat Ibn Wahban) clarifying that if the guardian gives charity and the owner appears, the guardian personally guarantees the value, not the child, so charity is permissible. Thus, the guardian may give charity without concern.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The legal guardian of a minor, responsible for managing the minor's affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when two people find a lost item, they must:
A) Each announce separately
B) Both announce and share the ruling
C) Only the first finder is responsible
D) They may decide between themselves who announces

Key Takeaway
Two finders must jointly announce and share all luqatah rulings.

Child Finder: Guardian's Role and Liability
Ruling with expansion on child finder.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the guardian's duties when a child finds a lost item and identify the liability if charity is given.

Core Idea
Guardian acts for child; charity is permissible but guardian bears liability if owner appears.

When a child finds a lost item, legal capacity is lacking, so the guardian steps in. This lesson explores the guardian's options after announcement, with a key nuance about giving charity to a stranger versus giving to the child, and the liability that follows.

Guided Path
1
Recognise the child finder's position
A child can find a lost item but lacks legal capacity to manage it. The guardian (wali or wasi) acts on the child's behalf.
The child is not neglected; the law safeguards his rights.
2
Understand the guardian's primary duty
The guardian must first announce the find, as any finder would.
Announcement is wajib; it protects the owner's chance to claim.
3
Explore the options after announcement
Guardian may keep the item, give it to the child (if poor), or give it in charity to a third party.
The text initially raises concern about giving charity due to potential harm.
4
Analyse the harm in giving charity
If the owner appears and the item is gone (given to a poor person), the guardian might have to compensate from the child's own wealth, which harms the child.
This is the reason for the initial hesitation.
5
Apply the later clarification
The commentary on Ibn Wahban's poem clarifies: if the guardian gives charity, the liability is on the guardian personally, not from the child's wealth. Thus, charity is permissible without harm.
This removes the earlier concern.

Source Text

Deputizing the Announcement of Found Property
Ruling on authorizing another to perform the announcement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on deputizing the announcement of found property and identify the condition that protects the finder from liability.

Core Idea
Deputizing the announcement is allowed if unable, but without judge's permission the finder remains liable.

When a finder of lost property cannot personally perform the announcement (ta'rif), may he appoint someone else? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two authoritative statements: one allowing deputization if the finder is unable, and another requiring the permission of the judge. Understanding this condition is crucial to avoid liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
The act is deputizing another person to perform the announcement of found property (istinaba fi al-ta'rif). Determine the general ruling from the sources cited.
2
Analyse the two statements
First, Abu al-Hasan in al-Tatar Khaniyya allows deputization if the finder is unable to announce himself. Second, al-Hawi al-Qudsi states that giving the item to another without the judge's permission subjects the finder to liability. Compare these conditions.
The first focuses on the finder's inability; the second on judicial oversight.
3
Synthesize the mufta bihi
The operative ruling: deputization is permissible, but to avoid liability the finder must obtain the judge's permission. The condition of inability is recommended but not legally required.
Later Hanafi practice often requires judge's permission to protect the finder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القاموس : التعريف الإعلام. وفي التتارخانية قال أبو الحسن : له أن يأمر غيره ويعطيها حتى يعرفها يريد إذا عجز عن التعريف بنفسه .اهـ. فأفاد جواز الاستنابة في التعريف لكن في الحاوي القدسي : لو دفعها إلى غيره بغير إذن القاضي ضمن اهـ .
In al-Qamus: Ta'rif means informing. In al-Tatar Khaniyya, Abu al-Hasan said: He may order another and give it to him so that he announces it, meaning if he is unable to announce himself. End quote. So it indicates the permissibility of deputizing in announcement. But in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: If he gives it to another without the permission of the judge, he is liable. End quote.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This short passage addresses whether a finder can appoint someone else to perform the announcement (ta'rif). Al-Qamus defines ta'rif as 'informing.' The Tatar Khaniyya quotes Abu al-Hasan who allows a finder to instruct another person and hand over the item for announcement if the finder himself is incapable. However, al-Hawi al-Qudsi sets a condition: such deputization is only valid with the permission of the judge; otherwise, the finder remains liable if the item is lost. This is a useful practical guideline for the finder who cannot personally announce.

Key Terms
الاستنابة (al-istinaba): Authorizing another person to perform the announcement on one's behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hawi al-Qudsi, what is required for the finder to deputize another for announcement without incurring liability?
A) The deputy must be a relative
B) The finder must be travelling
C) Permission of the judge
D) The item must be of little value

Key Takeaway
Deputizing the announcement is permissible, but to avoid liability the finder must obtain the judge's permission.
