Finder’s Spending: Volunteer Unless Authorized by Qadi
Explaining that the finder is a volunteer in spending unless the qadi permits with condition of reimbursement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the finder is a volunteer in spending and explain that only qadi's permission with condition of reimbursement makes it a debt.

Core Idea
Without qadi’s permission, finder is a volunteer — spending is charity, not debt.

This lesson examines the legal status of a finder (multaqit) who spends his own money on a foundling (laqit) or found item (luqata). The Hanafi school establishes that due to the finder's lack of guardianship (wilaya), he is a volunteer (mutabarri') unless the qadi authorizes spending with an explicit condition of reimbursement. We will explore the reasoning, the conditions, and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the foundling's later confirmation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The passage begins by stating that the finder is a volunteer in spending. Recognize this as the default: without any authorization, the finder cannot claim reimbursement.
This is analogous to paying someone else's debt without permission.
2
Recognize the lack of wilayah
The reason for the default rule is the finder's deficient guardianship over the foundling/found item. Contrast this with an executor (wasi) who has guardianship and can claim reimbursement if he testifies.
Wilayah is the key legal concept here.
3
Identify the exception with qadi's permission
The qadi has guardianship over absent persons and foundlings. If the qadi explicitly says 'Spend with the condition of reimbursement', the spending becomes a debt (dayn). The condition of reimbursement (an tarji') is essential.
A mere order without that condition is ambiguous and does not create a debt.
4
Understand the proof and dispute
The proof is qiyas (analogy): the finder is like a person paying another's debt without authorization. The passage also discusses Imam Muhammad's view that the foundling's later confirmation suffices, but the relied-upon position rejects this.
The analogy to manumission (mu'tiq) is rejected because manumission creates wala', which is a distinct legal relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وهو متبرع في الإنفاق على اللقيط واللقطة) أي الملتقط لقصور ولايته فصار كما لو قضى دين غيره بغير أمره قيد بالملتقط لأن الوصي لو أنفق عليه من مال ومال اليتيم غائب فهو متطوع إلا أن يشهد أنه قرض عليه أو أنه يرجع ولو اشترى له الوم طعاماً أو كسوة بشهادة شهود رجع ولو اشترى ثوباً أو خادماً لولده ونقد ثمنه من مال نفسه لا يرجع إلا أن يشهد أنه شراه له ليرجع ؛ كذا في جامع الفصولين من الفصل السابع والعشرين. وقيد حكم قضاء مديون الميت دينه بغير أمر وصيه وقضاء المودع دين مودعه بلا أمر وقضاء الوكيل بالبيع عن المشتري الثمن لموكله بلا أمره قوله : ( وبإذن القاضي يكون ديناً) لأن للقاضي ولاية في مال الغائب وعلى اللقيط نظراً لهما، وقد يكون النظر بالإنفاق وصورة إذن أن يقول له أنفق على أن ترجع فلو أمره به ولم يقل على أن ترجع لا يكون ديناً وهو لأن الأمر متردد بين الحسبة والرجوع فلا يكون ديناً بالشك. وعبارة المجمع أحسن وهي : فإن أنفق الملتقط كان متبرعاً إلا أن يأذن له القاضي بشرط الرجوع أو يصدقه اللقيط إذا بلغ اهـ. وينبغي أن يكون معنى التصديق تصديقه أنه أنفق عليه بأمر القاضي على أن لا تصديقه على الإنفاق لأنه لو كان بلا أمر القاضي لا رجوع عليه له فتصديقه وعدمه سواء. وفي شرحه لابن الملك خلافه فإنه قال : يعني إذا لم يأمر القاضي بإنفاقه فصدقه اللقيط بعد البلوغ أنه أنفقه للرجوع عليه فله الرجوع عليه لإقراره بحقه .اهـ. ولو صح هذا لزم أن يقال في الجواب فهو متبرع إلا أن يشهد أنه أنفق ليرجع أو يصدقه على ذلك وحينئذ لا اعتبار بأمر القاضي وهم قد اتفقوا على أنه لا بد من إذن القاضي لعدم ولاية الملتقط فلا يكفيه الإشهاد بخلاف الوصي لو أنفق من ماله وأشهد يرجع كما قدمناه لأن له ولاية في مال الأصح يرجع : في النهر بعد أن فسر الصحة بالجواز وأنت خبير بأن استعمال لفظ الصحة بمعنى المندوب مما لا يعرف في كلامهم وعلى ما قررنا جرى الشارح العيني ..هـ قلت: لا يخفى أن الصحة تجامع الإباحة والندب وغيرهما فلما كانت كذلك بين المؤلف أن المراد منها هنا الندب لما ،قاله ولا يتـ ا يتوهم أن المراد تفسیره معنى الصحة بما ذكره تفسيراً لغوياً أو عرفياً. قوله : فلو) وصف المصنف البهيمة بالضالة لكان أولى) قال في النهر : وعندي أن لفظ الالتقاط يغني عنه . قوله: (وأشهد يرجع) أي وإن فقد اليتيم، ولم أر من نبه على هذا المحل لكني فهمته مما نقلته عن الخانية في باب اللقيط عند قوله ونفقته في بيت المال. ولم يبين المصنف المديون لتعدده ففي اللقطة صاحبها، وفي اللقيط الأب إن ظهر له أب واللقيط بعد بلوغه إن لم يظهر له أب كما في الظهيرية، ومالكه إن ظهر له سيد بإقراره كما في الحاوي والعجب من الشارح أنه جعله صاحبها وسها عن اللقيط. ولم يذكر المصنف إقامة البينة من الملتقط قبل إذن القاضي وشرطه في الأصل وصححه في الهداية لأنه يحتمل أن يكون غصباً في يده ولا يأمر فيه بالإنفاق وإنما يأمره في الوديعة فلا بد من البينة لكشف الحال وليست تقام للقضاء حتى يشترط لها خصم لكن أنه في اللقطة، وأما في اللقيط فقد قدمنا أنه كذلك وصرح به في الظهيرية. وإن قال الملتقط لا بينة لي يقول له أنفق عليها إن كنت صادقاً. وفي الذخيرة: يقول له ذلك بين يدي الثقات. وكذا لو كانت اللقطة شيئاً يخاف عليه الهلاك متى لم ينفق عليه إلى إقامة البينة كما في الظهيرية. وقدمنا أن القاضي لو جعل ولاء اللقيط للملتقط جاز لأنه قضاء في فصل مجتهد فيه فإن من العلماء من قال بأن الملتقط يشبه المعتق من حيث إنه أحياه كالمعتق فعلى هذا لا يكون متبرعاً بالإنفاق بغير إذن القاضي إذا أشهد ليرجع كالوصي.
He said: (And he is a volunteer in spending on the foundling and the found item) meaning the finder because of his deficient guardianship, thus it is as if he paid the debt of another without his permission. He restricted it to the finder because the executor, if he spends from his wealth while the orphan's wealth is absent, he is a volunteer unless he testifies that it is a loan upon him or that he will reimburse. And if he buys food or clothing with witness testimony, he reimburses. And if he buys a garment or servant for his child and pays its price from his own wealth, he does not reimburse unless he testifies that he bought it for him to reimburse; thus in Jami' al-Fusulayn from the twenty-seventh chapter. And he restricted the ruling of paying the dead debtor's debt without the executor's permission, and the depositary's payment of the depositor's debt without permission, and the agent's payment of the buyer's price to his principal without his permission. He said: (And with the qadi's permission it becomes a debt) because the qadi has guardianship over the wealth of the absent and over the foundling out of consideration for them both, and consideration may be by spending. The form of permission is that he says to him: 'Spend with the condition that you reimburse.' If he just orders him without saying 'with reimbursement,' it is not a debt because the order is ambiguous between charity and reimbursement, so it is not a debt due to doubt. The expression of al-Majma' is better: 'Indeed the finder, if he spends, is a volunteer unless the qadi permits him with the condition of reimbursement, or the foundling confirms him when he reaches majority.' And the meaning of confirmation should be that he confirms that he spent by the qadi's order, not confirmation of the spending itself because without the qadi's order there is no recourse against him, so his confirmation and denial are equal. In Ibn al-Malik's commentary there is disagreement: he said it means if the qadi did not order spending, and the foundling after majority confirms that he spent for recourse, then he has recourse due to his acknowledgment of his right. If this were correct, it would be said in response: he is a volunteer unless he testifies that he spent to reimburse or the foundling confirms that, and then the qadi's order is irrelevant, but they have agreed that the qadi's order is necessary because the finder has no guardianship, so testimony is insufficient for him, unlike the guardian who, if he spends from his wealth and testifies, reimburses as we presented because he has guardianship over wealth. The correct is reimbursement: in al-Nahr after interpreting 'sahh' as permission, and you are aware that using 'sahh' to mean recommended is not known in their speech, and according to our verification proceeded al-Ayni. I say: it is not hidden that 'sahh' encompasses permissibility and recommendation and others, so when it is so, the author clarified that what is meant here is recommendation due to what he said, and lest one misunderstand that he intends to interpret the meaning of 'sahh' with what he mentioned as a linguistic or customary interpretation. He said: (then if) the author had described the animal as stray it would be better. He said in al-Nahr: in my view the word 'iltiqat' suffices. He said: (And he testifies to reimburse) meaning even if the orphan is missing, and I have not seen anyone point this out, but I understood it from what I quoted from al-Khaniyya in the chapter on the foundling at his saying 'and his maintenance is from the treasury.' And the author did not specify the debtor due to its multiplicity: in the found item it is its owner, in the foundling it is the father if a father appears, and the foundling after his majority if no father appears, as in al-Zahiriyya, and his owner if a master appears by his acknowledgment, as in al-Hawi. And it is surprising that the commentator made it its owner and forgot about the foundling. And the author did not mention establishing evidence by the finder before the qadi's permission, and its condition is in al-Asl and corrected in al-Hidayah because it could be a usurpation in his hand, and he does not order spending on it; rather he orders in the deposit, so evidence is needed to uncover the situation, and it is not established for judgment so a disputant is not required for it, but that is in the found item. As for the foundling, we have already presented that it is similar, and it is stated in al-Zahiriyya. And if the finder says 'I have no evidence,' he says to him: 'Spend on it if you are truthful.' And in al-Dhakhira: he says that to him in front of trustworthy people. Similarly, if the found item is something that fears perishing unless spent on until evidence is brought, as in al-Zahiriyya. And we have presented that if the qadi makes the foundling's patronage (wala') for the finder, it is permissible because it is a ruling in a matter of ijtihad, for some scholars say that the finder resembles the emancipator in that he gave it life like the emancipator; thus according to this, he is not a volunteer in spending without the qadi's permission if he testifies to reimburse, like the guardian.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding the finder's (multaqit) expenditure on the foundling (laqit) and the found item (luqata). The commentator explains that the finder is a volunteer (mutabarri') because he lacks guardianship (wilaya) over the foundling or the found item. This is analogous to a person paying another's debt without permission — he cannot claim reimbursement. However, if the qadi (judge) authorizes the spending with a condition of reimbursement, the expenditure becomes a debt (dayn) on the owner. The commentator cites various sources, including 'Jami' al-Fusulayn', to illustrate nuances: for example, an executor (wasi) who spends on an orphan may claim reimbursement if he testifies or if he explicitly states it as a loan. The qadi's permission must explicitly include 'on condition of reimbursement' (an tarji'), otherwise the order is ambiguous and no debt arises. There is also a discussion about the foundling later confirming the spending after majority: the correct view is that this confirmation is only valid if the qadi had authorized the spending; otherwise, the finder cannot claim reimbursement. The commentator then addresses the need for the finder to establish evidence (bayyina) that the item is truly lost and not usurped before the qadi authorizes spending. If the finder has no evidence, the qadi may still permit spending with careful inquiry. The passage also notes a minority view that the finder may be like a manumittor (mu'tiq) and hence not a volunteer, but the relied-upon position is that he remains a volunteer without qadi's permission.

Key Terms
متبرع (mutabarri'): A volunteer who spends without legal entitlement to reimbursement, akin to a charitable donor.
ولاية (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship over property or persons, enabling one to act on their behalf with legal effect.
إذن القاضي (idhn al-qadi): The permission of the judge (qadi) authorizing the finder to spend with the right of reimbursement, creating a debt on the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what condition is necessary for the finder (multaqit) to claim reimbursement for spending on a foundling?
A) The finder must have good intention
B) The foundling must later confirm the spending
C) The qadi must authorize the spending with condition of reimbursement
D) The finder must be a wealthy person

Key Takeaway
The finder is a volunteer unless the qadi explicitly permits with condition of reimbursement; without this, spending is charity, not debt.

Luqatah — Found Property
intermediate
8 min
Qadi's Discretion with Found Livestock: Hire or Sell
Qadi's options for found livestock and the dispute over runaway slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options the qadi has for a found stray animal, identify the condition that determines which option to choose, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding hiring a runaway slave.

Core Idea
If a stray animal has benefit, hire it; otherwise sell it — preserving the owner's property.

When a stray animal (bahima dalla) is found and brought to the qadi, the qadi must decide how to preserve the owner's property. The core ruling is simple: if the animal has some benefit (e.g., milk, wool, or labor), the qadi hires it out; if not, he sells it. But what about a runaway slave? This passage reveals an important intra-Hanafi dispute: can the qadi also hire out an abaq like a stray animal? Let's work through the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for a stray animal
The text states: 'If it has benefit, he hires it out and spends on it; otherwise he sells it.' Determine the legal operation: the qadi has two options—hire or sell—depending on the presence of benefit (naf').
This is a discretionary ruling based on preservation of the owner's property.
2
Understand the reason for the option of hiring
Hiring is preferred because it preserves the animal itself (ibqa' al-'ayn) for the owner without imposing a debt on him. The qadi can use the hire income for the animal's maintenance.
The purpose is to avoid burdening the owner with debt and to keep the asset intact.
3
Examine the exception for the runaway slave (abaq)
Some Hanafi sources say the qadi does not hire a runaway slave for fear he may run away again. But al-Hidayah makes no distinction, treating the abaq like the stray animal.
This is the point of contention within the school.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute and reconciliation
Sources like al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', and al-Khassa prohibit hiring the abaq; al-Hidayah and al-Kafi permit it. The commentator reconciles by conditioning permission on the lessee being strong/trustworthy or being informed of the slave's status.
The reconciled position: hiring is allowed if the lessee can secure the slave.
5
Note the open question about the foundling (laqit)
The author notes he has not seen a ruling for a foundling child who is discerning (mumayyiz) and has no wealth: can the qadi hire him out for work to cover expenses?
This remains an unresolved issue in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن كان لها نفع أجرها وأنفق (عليها أي اللقطة والمراد الضالة البهيمة لأن فيه إبقاء العين على مالكه من غير إلزام الدين عليه . قيد باللقطة لأن العبد الآبق لا يؤجره القاضي لأنه يخاف أن يأبق؛ كذا في التبيين. وفي الهداية: سوى بينهما بقوله وكذلك يفعل بالعبد الآبق ولم أر حكم اللقيط إذا صار مميزاً ولا مال له هل يؤجره القاضي للنفقة أو لا؟ قوله : (وإلا باعها أي إن لم يكن لها نفع باعها القاضي وحفظ ثمنها لصاحبها إبقاء له يعني عند تعذر إبقائه صورة وظاهر الكتاب أن القاضي يفعل أحد الأمرين من الإجارة إن أمكن وإلا فالبيع. وظاهره أنه إذا لم يكن له نفع لا يأذن له في الإنفاق وفي الهداية : وإن كان الأصلح الإنفاق عليها أذن في ذلك وجعل النفقة ديناً على مالكها. قالوا: إنما يأمر بالإنفاق 1 إذن القاضي. قوله : (وفي الهداية سوى بينهما قال في حواشي مسكين: واعلم أنه اختلف في الآبق هل يؤجر كالضال أولا ؟ ففي الهداية والكافي نعم قال في الدرر : ولم أجده في غيرهما بل وجدت في المحيط والبدائع والخاصة خلافه حيث قالوا: لا يجوز إجارة الآبق لاحتمال أن يأبق، ووفق بحمل ما في الهداية والكافي على ما إذا كان المستأجر ذا قوة ومنعة لا يخاف عليه عنده وما في غيرهما على خلافه، أو بحمل كلامهما على الإيجار مع إعلام المستأجر بحاله ليحفظ غاية الحفظ وما في غيرهما على الإيجار مع جهله بحاله شرنبلالية عن المقدسي.
He said: (And if it has benefit, he hires it out and spends on it) meaning the found item, and what is intended is the stray animal (dallah bahima) because in that is preservation of the commodity for its owner without imposing a debt upon him. He restricted it to the found item because the runaway slave (abaq) the qadi does not hire him out because he fears he may run away; thus in al-Tabyin. And in al-Hidayah: he made them equal by his saying: 'And similarly he does with the runaway slave.' And I have not seen the ruling of the foundling when he becomes discerning (mumayyiz) and has no wealth: does the qadi hire him out for maintenance or not? He said: (And otherwise he sells it) meaning if it has no benefit, the qadi sells it and preserves its price for its owner to preserve [the value] for him, meaning when preservation of its form is impossible. The apparent meaning of the book is that the qadi does one of two things: hire if possible, otherwise sell. And its apparent meaning is that if it has no benefit, he does not permit spending on it. And in al-Hidayah: 'If the most beneficial (aslah) is to spend on it, he permits that and makes the maintenance a debt on its owner.' They said: He only orders spending [with] the qadi's permission. He said: (And in al-Hidayah he made them equal.) He said in Hawashi Miskin: 'Know that there is disagreement regarding the runaway slave: is he hired like the stray or not? In al-Hidayah and al-Kafi, yes. He said in al-Durar: I did not find it in other than them, rather I found in al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', and al-Khassa the opposite: they said it is not permissible to hire the runaway slave because of the possibility that he may run away. And reconciliation is by carrying what is in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi to the case when the lessee is a person of strength and security not fearing [escape] from him, and what is in others to the opposite, or by carrying their words on hiring with informing the lessee of his state so he preserves him with utmost care, and what is in others on hiring without his knowledge of the state.' [This is] from the Sharnablaliyya from al-Maqdisi.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage discusses the qadi's options when dealing with found livestock (dallah bahima). The finder brings the animal to the qadi, who may either hire it out (ujuurah) if the animal has some benefit (e.g., milk, wool, or labor) that can generate income without selling the animal, or sell it if it has no benefit or if selling is more beneficial. The goal is to preserve the animal's value for its owner without burdening the finder with expenses. The ruling is specifically for found items that are animals; a runaway slave (abaq) is different: some scholars (like those of al-Tabyin) hold that the qadi should not hire him out for fear of escape, but al-Hidayah equates the two, suggesting the qadi can hire the slave if there is a reliable lessee. The commentary then addresses a dispute: some sources (al-Muhit, al-Bada'i') prohibit hiring a runaway slave due to escape risk, while al-Hidayah and al-Kafi allow it. The author attempts reconciliation: the permission applies if the lessee is strong and can guard the slave, or if the lessee is informed of the slave's status so he takes precautions. The passage ends with a query about the foundling (laqit) who reaches discerning age (mumayyiz) but has no wealth: can the qadi hire him out for work to cover his expenses? The author notes he has not seen a definitive ruling on this, leaving it as an open question.

Key Terms
بهيمة ضالة (bahima dalla): A stray domestic animal (livestock) that is lost and found by someone.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hire/lease whereby the qadi rents out the found animal to someone for a fee, preserving the owner's property.
آبق (abaq): A runaway slave (male or female) who has escaped from his/her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary factor that determines whether the qadi hires out or sells a found stray animal?
A) The animal's age
B) Whether the animal has any beneficial use
C) The finder's preference
D) The owner's religion

Key Takeaway
The qadi preserves the owner's property by hiring if the animal has benefit, selling if not; for a runaway slave, hiring is allowed with a reliable lessee.

Hiring the Foundling Who Becomes Discerning: Unresolved Issue
A query about hiring a discerning foundling for maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the unresolved question regarding hiring out a discerning foundling and state the reasoning for its permissibility based on analogy.

Core Idea
A foundling's labor may be hired out for his own maintenance, but the proceeds belong solely to him—not to the finder or qadi.

This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq raises a practical question: what happens when a foundling (laqit) reaches the age of discernment (tamyiz) but still has no property? Can the qadi hire him out so that he can earn his own living? The author admits he has not seen a definitive ruling, then transmits a useful analogy from earlier Hanafi works. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the unresolved nature of the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
Read the first line: the author asks whether the qadi can hire out a discerning foundling who has no wealth for his maintenance. Identify the key elements: foundling (laqit), discernment (mumayyiz), no wealth, hiring out (ijarah).
2
Locate the authorities cited
The author quotes Abu al-Su'ud, who references al-Qahistani. Understand their roles: Abu al-Su'ud is a later Hanafi commentator; al-Qahistani is an earlier authority. Their statements provide the basis for the analogy.
3
Trace the analogy
Abu al-Su'ud argues: since the finder (muttalaqit) is permitted to hire out the foundling provided the wages go to the foundling, the qadi—who has guardianship—should also be permitted. Identify the common ground: both act as guardians for the foundling's benefit.
The analogy is based on the principle of 'guardianship for benefit' (wilayah al-maslahah).
4
Recognize the open issue
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq states he has not seen a definitive ruling (ma lam ara). Note that this remains an unresolved issue (mas'alah ghayr muhakkamah), indicating space for ijtihad or reliance on the cited analogy.
In Hanafi fatwa practice, unresolved issues are often decided by qiyas or istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم أر حكم اللقيط إذا صار مميزاً ولا مال له هل يؤجره القاضي للنفقة أو لا؟) قال أبو السعود أقول : إذا جاز للملتقط أن يؤجره لتكون الأجرة للقيط كما يستفاد مما سبق عن القهستاني حيث قال : وليس له أن يؤجره ليأخذ الأجرة لنفسه فكذا القاضي وتعليلهم المنع
He said: (And I have not seen the ruling of the foundling when he becomes discerning (mumayyiz) and has no wealth: does the qadi hire him out for maintenance or not?) Abu al-Su'ud said: I say: If it is permissible for the finder to hire him out so that the hire goes to the foundling, as is understood from what preceded from al-Qahistani where he said: 'It is not permissible for him to hire him out to take the hire for himself,' so likewise the qadi, and their reasoning for prohibition [is omitted].
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This short passage raises a query about a foundling (laqit) who has reached the age of discernment (tamyiz) but possesses no wealth. The question is whether the qadi can hire out this foundling for work, with the wages being used for his maintenance. The author of al-Bahr al-Rai'q states that he has not seen a definitive ruling on this matter. He then quotes Abu al-Su'ud who references al-Qahistani: the finder is allowed to hire out the foundling only if the wages go to the foundling (not to the finder). By analogy, the qadi should also be able to do so, since the qadi acts in the foundling's best interest. The text ends abruptly, but the implication is that the permissibility is likely, as the qadi has guardianship over the foundling. However, the author does not give a final fatwa, indicating this is an area requiring further research or ijtihad.

Key Terms
مميز (mumayyiz): A child who has reached the age of discernment (typically around 7 years) and can understand basic transactions and concepts, though not legally mature (baligh).
لقيط (laqit): A foundling, an abandoned child of unknown parentage, who is cared for by the community or a finder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To generate profit for the finder
B) To provide for the foundling's maintenance
C) To punish the foundling
D) To teach him a trade

Key Takeaway
The hiring out of a discerning foundling is permissible only when the wages are used for his own maintenance, and the guardian cannot benefit personally.
